<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">R. Madhavan</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em">

</tr>
<tr>

<td><span class="nickname">Madhavan Balaji Ranganathan</span><br/>
<span style="display:none">(<span class="bday">1970-06-01</span>)</span> 1 June 1970 <span class="noprint ForceAgeToShow">(age 46)</span><br/>
<span class="birthplace"><a href="/wiki/Jamshedpur" title="Jamshedpur">Jamshedpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> (now in <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>) , India</span></td>

<td>Sarita Birje (1999–present)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Ranganathan Madhavan</b> (born 1 June 1970) is an Indian actor, writer and film producer. Madhavan has received two <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards_South" title="Filmfare Awards South">Filmfare Awards</a>, an award from the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu_State_Film_Awards" title="Tamil Nadu State Film Awards">Tamil Nadu State Film Awards</a> alongside recognition and nominations from other organisations. He has been described as one of the few actors in India who is able to achieve pan-Indian appeal, appearing in films from seven different languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pan-Indian_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-pan-Indian-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-language_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-language-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan began his acting career with television guest appearances, including a role on the <a href="/wiki/Zee_TV" title="Zee TV">Zee TV</a> prime-time soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/Banegi_Apni_Baat" title="Banegi Apni Baat">Banegi Apni Baat</a></i> in 1996. After appearing in commercials and in small roles, he later gained <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_role" title="Breakthrough role">recognition</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">Tamil film industry</a> through <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a>'s successful romance film <i><a href="/wiki/Alaipayuthey" title="Alaipayuthey">Alaipayuthey</a></i> (2000). Madhavan soon developed an image as a romantic hero with notable roles in two of 2001's highest grossing Tamil films, <a href="/wiki/Gautham_Menon" title="Gautham Menon">Gautham Menon</a>'s directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/Minnale" title="Minnale">Minnale</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Madras_Talkies" title="Madras Talkies">Madras Talkies</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Dumm_Dumm_Dumm" title="Dumm Dumm Dumm">Dumm Dumm Dumm</a></i>. He worked with Mani Ratnam again in the critically acclaimed 2002 film <i><a href="/wiki/Kannathil_Muthamittal" title="Kannathil Muthamittal">Kannathil Muthamittal</a></i> playing the father of an adopted girl, whilst he achieved commercial success with his role in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N._Linguswamy" title="N. Linguswamy">N. Linguswamy</a>'s action film, <i><a href="/wiki/Run_(2002_film)" title="Run (2002 film)">Run</a></i> (2002).</p>
<p>Madhavan was cast alongside <a href="/wiki/Kamal_Haasan" title="Kamal Haasan">Kamal Haasan</a> in the 2003 drama <i><a href="/wiki/Anbe_Sivam" title="Anbe Sivam">Anbe Sivam</a></i>, which earned him two notable awards for Best Supporting Actor. In 2004, he gave a critically acclaimed performance as the antagonist in the multi-starrer <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aayutha_Ezhuthu" title="Aayutha Ezhuthu">Aayutha Ezhuthu</a></i> and the film secured him his first <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards_South" title="Filmfare Awards South">Filmfare Award</a> for the intense portrayal of a rogue. In the mid-2000s, Madhavan also actively pursued a career in <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Hindi films</a>, by appearing in supporting roles in three highly successful productions, <a href="/wiki/Rakeysh_Omprakash_Mehra" title="Rakeysh Omprakash Mehra">Rakeysh Omprakash Mehra</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rang_De_Basanti" title="Rang De Basanti">Rang De Basanti</a></i> (2006), Mani Ratnam's biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_(2007_film)" title="Guru (2007 film)">Guru</a></i> (2007) and <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> (2009), which went on to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Indian_films" title="List of highest-grossing Indian films">highest grossing Indian film of all time</a> upon release. He simultaneously worked on Tamil films, gaining critical acclaim for his portrayal of a <a href="/wiki/Vigilante" title="Vigilante">vigilante</a> in his home production <i><a href="/wiki/Evano_Oruvan" title="Evano Oruvan">Evano Oruvan</a></i> (2007) and for the successful bilingual horror film, <i><a href="/wiki/Yavarum_Nalam" title="Yavarum Nalam">Yavarum Nalam</a></i> (2009). After appearing in further box office hits, <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i> (2011) and <i><a href="/wiki/Vettai" title="Vettai">Vettai</a></i> (2012), Madhavan took a break from acting. Returning after a three-year sabbatical in 2015, his comeback films, the romantic-comedy <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu_Returns" title="Tanu Weds Manu Returns">Tanu Weds Manu Returns</a></i> (2015) and the sports drama <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Irudhi Suttru</a></i> (2016), both won critical and commercial acclaim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to his acting career, Madhavan has worked as a writer on his films, hosted television programmes and has been a prominent celebrity endorser for brands and products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oragadam_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-oragadam-5">[5]</a></sup> He has also worked as a film producer, first making <i>Evano Oruvan</i> with Leukos Films, before setting up Tricolour Films to produce <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Saala Khadoos</a></i> (2016). Madhavan is noted for his philanthropic activities and promotes various causes such as environment, health and education. He is particularly vocal about the protection of animals and was awarded PETA's Person of the Year recognition in 2012.</p>
<p></p>
