<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Madhavan was born on 1 June 1970 in <a href="/wiki/Jamshedpur" title="Jamshedpur">Jamshedpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> (now in <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>), India, to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_people" title="Tamil people">Tamil</a> family. His father Ranganathan was a management executive in <a href="/wiki/Tata_Steel" title="Tata Steel">Tata Steel</a> and his mother, Saroja was a manager in the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_India" title="Bank of India">Bank of India</a>. His younger sister, Devika, is a software engineer settled in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-family_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-family-6">[6]</a></sup> He had a Tamil-speaking upbringing in <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tambrahm_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-tambrahm-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1988, Madhavan gained a scholarship to represent India as a cultural ambassador from Rajaram College, <a href="/wiki/Kolhapur" title="Kolhapur">Kolhapur</a> and spent a year in <a href="/wiki/Stettler,_Alberta" title="Stettler, Alberta">Stettler, Alberta</a>, Canada as part of an exchange programme. He returned to Kolhapur and completed his education, graduating with a degree in electronics. During his college years, Madhavan became actively involved in extra-curricular military training and at 22, he was recognised as amongst the leading <a href="/wiki/National_Cadet_Corps_(India)" title="National Cadet Corps (India)">NCC</a> cadets in <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>, which allowed him to make a trip with seven others as <a href="/wiki/National_Cadet_Corps_(India)" title="National Cadet Corps (India)">NCC</a> cadets to England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twm2015_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-twm2015-8">[8]</a></sup> As a result of this opportunity, he received training with the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, which he had, at a point, considered joining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cadet_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-cadet-9">[9]</a></sup> However he missed the age cut-off by six months and was subsequently unable to join the programme. After he lost out on the place, he began teaching courses on public speaking and personality development skills in Kolhapur and the satisfaction he gained through teaching, prompted him to pursue a post-graduation in public speaking at <a href="/wiki/Kishinchand_Chellaram_College" title="Kishinchand Chellaram College">Kishinchand Chellaram College</a> in Mumbai. During the period, he also won the Indian Championship for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Speaking" title="Public Speaking">Public Speaking</a> and subsequently represented India at the Young Businessmen Conference in Tokyo, Japan in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-speak_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-speak-10">[10]</a></sup> During his stint in Mumbai, he opted to create a portfolio and submit it to a modelling agency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twm2015_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-twm2015-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_work">Early work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 1996, Madhavan worked on a sandalwood talc advertisement directed by <a href="/wiki/Santosh_Sivan" title="Santosh Sivan">Santosh Sivan</a>, who later recommended him to <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a> to take part in a screen test for a role in <i><a href="/wiki/Iruvar" title="Iruvar">Iruvar</a></i> (1997). Madhavan was auditioned for the leading role of Tamizhselvan amongst several other more established actors, but Mani Ratnam eventually left him out of the project citing that he thought his "eyes looked too young" for a senior role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iruvar_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-iruvar-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iruvargold_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-iruvargold-12">[12]</a></sup> As his film career failed to take off, Madhavan went on to feature in Hindi television serials, appearing as a crook in his first venture <i>Yule Love Stories</i>. He appeared in leading roles in <a href="/wiki/Zee_TV" title="Zee TV">Zee TV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Banegi_Apni_Baat" title="Banegi Apni Baat">Banegi Apni Baat</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ghar_Jamai_(TV_series)" title="Ghar Jamai (TV series)">Ghar Jamai</a></i>, while he gained further popularity portraying the character of Shekhar in <i><a href="/wiki/Saaya_(TV_series)" title="Saaya (TV series)">Saaya</a></i>. He also went on to act as a ship's captain in <i><a href="/wiki/Sea_Hawks_(TV_series)" title="Sea Hawks (TV series)">Sea Hawks</a></i>, as a convict in <i>Yeh Kahan Aa Gaye Hum</i> and as worked as a television anchor in <i>Tol Mol Ke Bol</i> amongst other television appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-serials_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-serials-13">[13]</a></sup> His first appearance in a feature film role came through a small role in <i><a href="/wiki/Is_Raat_Ki_Subah_Nahin" title="Is Raat Ki Subah Nahin">Is Raat Ki Subah Nahin</a></i> (1996), where he portrayed a singer in a bar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, Madhavan appeared in a supporting role as an Indian police officer in <a href="/wiki/Fred_Olen_Ray" title="Fred Olen Ray">Fred Olen Ray</a>'s English film, <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(1997_film)" title="Inferno (1997 film)">Inferno</a></i>, which was shot in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iruvargold_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-iruvargold-12">[12]</a></sup> His first chance in <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India" title="Cinema of India">Indian cinema</a> came in the form of <i><a href="/wiki/Shanti_Shanti_Shanti" title="Shanti Shanti Shanti">Shanti Shanti Shanti</a></i> (1998), a <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a> film, in which he appeared as a carefree youngster alongside actor <a href="/wiki/Abbas_(actor)" title="Abbas (actor)">Abbas</a>. However, the film failed to make an impact and went unnoticed at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sss_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-sss-15">[15]</a></sup> During the period, Hindi film director Vinod Pandey launched Madhavan as a <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> hero, with a project titled <i><a href="/wiki/Akeli_(film)" title="Akeli (film)">Akeli</a></i>, however the film was shelved before the production process had been completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lakheli_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-lakheli-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932003">1999–2003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1999–2003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1999, leading Indian director <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a> selected Madhavan to feature in the leading role of his Tamil romantic film, <i><a href="/wiki/Alaipayuthey" title="Alaipayuthey">Alaipayuthey</a></i> (2000) and the film's subsequent critical and commercial success gave Madhavan his <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_role" title="Breakthrough role">breakthrough</a> as an actor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iruvargold_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-iruvargold-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alai_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-alai-17">[17]</a></sup> Portraying the character of Karthik Varadharajan, a young husband experiencing difficulties with his marriage, Madhavan revealed that he studied the technical aspects of film-making from the director and learned the entire script of the film, irrespective of whether he was in the scene or not. He became the first débutante actor to be cast by Mani Ratnam in the lead role of a film, and revealed that when he found out that he was set to work with the director he was overcome with a "mixture of excitement, awe, fear and expectations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Featuring alongside actress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shalini" title="Shalini">Shalini</a>, Madhavan's performance was well received by critics and the film's success led to it developing "classic" status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bebe_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-bebe-19">[19]</a></sup> A critic from <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a>, described that Madhavan "sails through the litmus test with ease", whilst another review cited that Madhavan was a "promising debutant" into the film industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aphindu_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-aphindu-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apindo_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-apindo-21">[21]</a></sup> After the success of his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_film" title="Tamil film">Tamil film</a>, the producers of his previous <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a> film, <i>Shanti Shanti Shanti</i>, dubbed the film into Tamil and released it as <i>Relax</i>, to capitalise on Madhavan's new-found success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sss_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-sss-15">[15]</a></sup> Madhavan's next film, <i><a href="/wiki/Ennavale" title="Ennavale">Ennavale</a></i> (2000), garnered mixed reviews although Madhavan's portrayal was praised as the "mainstay" of the film, with claims that the film for him was a "merely a prosaic exercise".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enhindu_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-enhindu-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan's first release of 2001, <a href="/wiki/Gautham_Menon" title="Gautham Menon">Gautham Menon</a>'s directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/Minnale" title="Minnale">Minnale</a></i>, opened to critical and commercial acclaim. Featuring a popular soundtrack by <a href="/wiki/Harris_Jayaraj" title="Harris Jayaraj">Harris Jayaraj</a> and marketed as a <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a> release, <i>Minnale</i> further built on the actor's image as a <a href="/wiki/Romantic_hero" title="Romantic hero">romantic hero</a> and was later listed as a "classic romantic film" from the Tamil film industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minhindu_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-minhindu-24">[24]</a></sup> He then collaborated with Mani Ratnam for the second time by appearing in the director's production venture, the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Dumm_Dumm_Dumm" title="Dumm Dumm Dumm">Dumm Dumm Dumm</a></i> (2001), alongside <a href="/wiki/Jyothika" title="Jyothika">Jyothika</a>. Appearing as an unhappy groom trying to halt his wedding, the film won positive acclaim and became a commercial success, with Madhavan establishing himself as a bankable actor in <a href="/wiki/South_India" title="South India">South India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twohits_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-twohits-25">[25]</a></sup> Madhavan then again appeared as a husband in a tumultuous marriage in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parthale_Paravasam" title="Parthale Paravasam">Parthale Paravasam</a></i> (2001), the hundredth venture of veteran director <a href="/wiki/K._Balachander" title="K. Balachander">K. Balachander</a>. Despite featuring amongst an ensemble cast and being highly anticipated prior to release, the film failed at the box-office, with critics citing that Madhavan looked "rather bored" with the proceedings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paravasam_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-paravasam-26">[26]</a></sup> Similarly his first lead role in a Hindi film, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rehna_Hai_Tere_Dil_Mein" title="Rehna Hai Tere Dil Mein">Rehna Hai Tere Dil Mein</a></i> (2001), a remake of his <i>Minnale</i>, was also unsuccessful at the box office, with the film and Madhavan's performance receiving mixed reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhtdmreview_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-rhtdmreview-27">[27]</a></sup> However, the film belatedly gained popularity through screenings on television and subsequently developed a cult following amongst young audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, Madhavan played the role of a novelist in Mani Ratnam's <i><a href="/wiki/Kannathil_Muthamittal" title="Kannathil Muthamittal">Kannathil Muthamittal</a></i> alongside actresses <a href="/wiki/P._S._Keerthana" title="P. S. Keerthana">Keerthana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simran_(actress)" title="Simran (actress)">Simran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nandita_Das" title="Nandita Das">Nandita Das</a>. In the film, he was shown as the role of the father of an adopted child, who wishes to return to her native homeland amidst the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_civil_war" title="Sri Lankan civil war">Sri Lankan civil war</a>. The film received widespread critical acclaim and went on to win six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Awards</a> as well as over ten awards at various International Film Festivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-km_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-km-29">[29]</a></sup> Madhavan gained acclaim for his portrayal with a critic citing "he lived the role of the character he portrays", with the film seeing him move away from the romantic hero image for the first time into a more serious, performance-orientated role. The good performance of the film internationally also helped him develop an overseas market for his films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kmreview_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-kmreview-31">[31]</a></sup> Madhavan's next large success came with <i><a href="/wiki/Run_(2002_film)" title="Run (2002 film)">Run</a></i>, a film recognised for its screenplay, with Madhavan appearing in an action film for the first time in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-run_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-run-32">[32]</a></sup> In regard to his performance, <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a>'s critic noted "he manages to portray action with élan in <i>Run</i> and actually looks fit and comfortable in the role", with the film helping him make a breakthrough as an <a href="/wiki/Action_hero" title="Action hero">action hero</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Despite another unsuccessful Hindi venture with the musical, <i><a href="/wiki/Dil_Vil_Pyar_Vyar" title="Dil Vil Pyar Vyar">Dil Vil Pyar Vyar</a></i> (2002), the success of his previous films helped him secure the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu_State_Film_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Tamil Nadu State Film Award for Best Actor">Tamil Nadu State Film Award for Best Actor</a> for 2002, being jointly recognised for both films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awardstwo_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-awardstwo-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan was cast alongside <a href="/wiki/Kamal_Haasan" title="Kamal Haasan">Kamal Haasan</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Anbe_Sivam" title="Anbe Sivam">Anbe Sivam</a></i> (2003), which told the story of an unexpected journey from <a href="/wiki/Bhubaneswar" title="Bhubaneswar">Bhubaneswar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> of two men who are polar opposites. Madhavan revealed his elation at working with an experienced actor like Kamal Haasan, while noting that a human drama film like <i>Anbe Sivam</i> was important for his career as an actor as it came after a successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masala_(film_genre)" title="Masala (film genre)">masala</a> film in <i>Run</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Portraying a young frustrated filmmaker with capitalist beliefs who travels with a handicapped communist played by Kamal Haasan, Madhavan's performance was described as a "milestone in his career" and that "his portrayal will remain with the viewer for long" by a critic from <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sivamhin_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-sivamhin-37">[37]</a></sup> The film opened in January 2003 to positive reviews, but became a surprise box-office failure. Post-release, the film has garnered belated critical acclaim from critics and television audiences and is considered as one of the "cult classics" of Tamil cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Baradwaj_Rangan" title="Baradwaj Rangan">Baradwaj Rangan</a> wrote that the film "was leagues ahead of the average Tamil and Indian film", though felt that "the masses were unwilling to accept the experimental nature of the film", while talking about the film's box office failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sivam_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-sivam-41">[41]</a></sup> Post-filming, Kamal Haasan revealed that he was impressed with Madhavan's enthusiasm and concentration during the making of the film and thus subsequently signed him on to appear in his production venture, <i><a href="/wiki/Nala_Damayanthi" title="Nala Damayanthi">Nala Damayanthi</a></i> (2003), where he played a <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">Brahmin</a> <a href="/wiki/Cook_(profession)" title="Cook (profession)">cook</a> lost in Australia. In 2003, the actor also appeared in <a href="/wiki/Vikraman" title="Vikraman">Vikraman</a>'s family drama <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Priyamana_Thozhi" title="Priyamana Thozhi">Priyamana Thozhi</a></i> as a budding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cricketer" title="Cricketer">cricketer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saran_(director)" title="Saran (director)">Saran</a>'s romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Jay_Jay" title="Jay Jay">Jay Jay</a></i> and made a guest appearance in <a href="/wiki/Priyadarshan" title="Priyadarshan">Priyadarshan</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lesa_Lesa" title="Lesa Lesa">Lesa Lesa</a></i> as a jailed teacher. The three films made average returns at the box office, though Madhavan's performances were appreciated by critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twoflops_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-twoflops-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ndreview_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-ndreview-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jjreview_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-jjreview-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.932008">2004–2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2004–2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madhavan played an imposter gangster in <a href="/wiki/K._S._Ravikumar" title="K. S. Ravikumar">K. S. Ravikumar</a>'s comedy <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aethiree" title="Aethiree">Aethiree</a></i> (2004) before being selected to feature in his fourth Mani Ratnam production, <i><a href="/wiki/Aaytha_Ezhuthu" title="Aaytha Ezhuthu">Aaytha Ezhuthu</a></i> (2004), which featured him in an ensemble cast including <a href="/wiki/Suriya" title="Suriya">Suriya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siddharth_(actor)" title="Siddharth (actor)">Siddharth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meera_Jasmine" title="Meera Jasmine">Meera Jasmine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esha_Deol" title="Esha Deol">Esha Deol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trisha_(actress)" title="Trisha (actress)">Trisha</a>. Madhavan portrayed the character of Inba Sekhar, a hitman living in the slums of <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, whose path crosses with the characters portrayed by Suriya and Siddharth. His role also featured him in a struggling marriage, where his wife desperately tries to claw him away from his profession. Madhavan bulked up and sported a shaven look for the first time in his career to resemble the character of a ruffian and shot for the film through the sync sound technique.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aayutha_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-aayutha-45">[45]</a></sup> He received widespread praise for his depiction, with Baradwaj Rangan of The Hindu claiming that Madhavan outplayed <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Bachchan" title="Abhishek Bachchan">Abhishek Bachchan</a>'s interpretation of the character in the Hindi version of the bilingual, <i><a href="/wiki/Yuva" title="Yuva">Yuva</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ezhuthu_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-ezhuthu-46">[46]</a></sup> Madhavan went on to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filmfare_Best_Supporting_Actor_Award_(Tamil)" title="Filmfare Best Supporting Actor Award (Tamil)">Filmfare Award for the Best Tamil Supporting Actor</a>, whilst another critic from The Hindu cited that he "sparkles as an anti-hero" and that the "character ought to find a very special place in his repertoire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aereview_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-aereview-47">[47]</a></sup> Similarly, a critic from Indiaglitz.com stated "Madhavan's daring decision to play a negative character, who gets beaten up black and blue at the end, putting his 'hero' image in peril, has paid off, as he walks away with top honours", while a reviewer from Sify.com labelled him as "terrific".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In late 2004, Madhavan worked on <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Anchal" title="Rajiv Anchal">Rajiv Anchal</a>'s English-Malayalam crossover film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nothing_But_Life" title="Nothing But Life">Nothing But Life</a></i> (2005) and completed his work in a single schedule across <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albuquerque" title="Albuquerque">Albuquerque</a>. Portraying an orphaned youth with suicidal tendencies being treated by a Malayali psychiatrist in the USA, the film and his portrayal opened to mixed reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top10review_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-top10review-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-innbl_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-innbl-51">[51]</a></sup> He then appeared in another marriage drama film, <i><a href="/wiki/Priyasakhi" title="Priyasakhi">Priyasakhi</a></i> (2005) co-starring <a href="/wiki/Sadha" title="Sadha">Sadha</a> – with the pair playing an estranged husband and wife. The film received praise for the lead pair's performances with Madhavan being praised as "top class", while it also became the first <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> film to be dubbed into <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zulu_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-zulu-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psreview_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-psreview-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2005 onwards, Madhavan increased his work in Hindi films and starred and wrote the Hindi dialogues for the comedy <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramji_Londonwaley" title="Ramji Londonwaley">Ramji Londonwaley</a></i> (2005), a remake of his earlier film <i>Nala Damayanthi</i>. Critics described his performance as "a master stroke", though the film fared averagely at the box office due to the release of other big budget films during the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rlreview_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-rlreview-54">[54]</a></sup> He experienced box office success in Hindi films for the first time through his role in <a href="/wiki/Rakeysh_Omprakash_Mehra" title="Rakeysh Omprakash Mehra">Rakeysh Omprakash Mehra</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rang_De_Basanti" title="Rang De Basanti">Rang De Basanti</a></i> (2006). Featuring in an ensemble cast led by <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a>, Madhavan essayed the guest role of <a href="/wiki/Flight_lieutenant" title="Flight lieutenant">flight lieutenant</a>, whose death triggers a revolutionary movement against corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cadet_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-cadet-9">[9]</a></sup> The film was subsequently nominated for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Film" title="BAFTA Award for Best Foreign Film">Best Foreign Language Film</a> at the 2006 <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA Awards</a>, while it was also chosen as India's official entry for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Awards</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_submissions_to_the_79th_Academy_Awards_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="List of submissions to the 79th Academy Awards for Best Foreign Language Film">Academy Awards</a> for the Best Foreign Language Film category. Madhavan then collaborated with Mani Ratnam for the fifth time with in the biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_(2007_film)" title="Guru (2007 film)">Guru</a></i> (2007), co-starring <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Bachchan" title="Abhishek Bachchan">Abhishek Bachchan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aishwarya_Rai" title="Aishwarya Rai">Aishwarya Rai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vidya_Balan" title="Vidya Balan">Vidya Balan</a>. His role of Shyam Saxena was inspired from the life of real-life journalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._Gurumurthy" title="S. Gurumurthy">S. Gurumurthy</a>, who was a challenger to the business tycoon, <a href="/wiki/Dhirubhai_Ambani" title="Dhirubhai Ambani">Dhirubhai Ambani</a>, whose life drew allusions with Bachchan's role. The film became a blockbuster and also received critical acclaim, with a reviewer citing that Madhavan acts with "extreme, believable sincerity" dubbing him as "truly a poster boy for India", whilst another claimed he performed "a weak role with élan".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gurureview_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-gurureview-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gurureviewsen_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-gurureviewsen-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>His Tamil film, <i><a href="/wiki/Thambi" title="Thambi">Thambi</a></i> (2006) directed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seeman_(director)" title="Seeman (director)">Seeman</a>, had a delayed release but became a profitable venture in town and village centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thambirediff_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-thambirediff-57">[57]</a></sup> Madhavan's portrayal of a rustic do-gooder, received positive reviews from critics though a reviewer from The Hindu claimed the actor was "unable to shed off his classy looks".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thambibad_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-thambibad-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thambigood_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-thambigood-59">[59]</a></sup> He then appeared in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sundar_C" title="Sundar C">Sundar C</a>'s comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Rendu" title="Rendu">Rendu</a></i> (2006), where he played dual roles for the first time and in the long-delayed romantic comedy <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arya_(2007_film)" title="Arya (2007 film)">Aarya</a></i> (2007), appearing as a medical student.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aryareview_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-aryareview-60">[60]</a></sup> Madhavan wrote the dialogues, produced and featured in the lead role in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nishikanth_Kamat" title="Nishikanth Kamat">Nishikanth Kamat</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Evano_Oruvan" title="Evano Oruvan">Evano Oruvan</a></i> (2007), playing a middle class bank employee who becomes so disgusted with the corruption he faces in his day-to-day life that he becomes a vigilante. After setting up a production studio, Leukos Films, he helped promote the film in international film festivals before the theatrical release in December 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoprom_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-eoprom-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eopromtwo_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-eopromtwo-62">[62]</a></sup> Critics called the film a "must watch" and a reviewer from <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a> stated that the film was "Madhavan's best performance to date", while he also went on to win the <a href="/wiki/ITFA_Best_Actor_Award" title="ITFA Best Actor Award">ITFA Best Actor Award</a> for his depiction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoreviews_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-eoreviews-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoreview2_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-eoreview2-64">[64]</a></sup> However <i>Evano Oruvan</i> and his subsequent release, Seeman's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vaazhthukal" title="Vaazhthukal">Vaazhthukal</a></i> (2008) did not perform well at the box office, while another completed film titled <i><a href="/wiki/Naan_Aval_Adhu" title="Naan Aval Adhu">Naan Aval Adhu</a></i> failed to have a theatrical release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vrreview2_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-vrreview2-65">[65]</a></sup> Madhavan's final release of the year was the docudrama <i><a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Meri_Jaan" title="Mumbai Meri Jaan">Mumbai Meri Jaan</a></i>, based upon the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Mumbai_Bombings" title="2006 Mumbai Bombings">2006 Mumbai Bombings</a>. The film, which featured him alongside <a href="/wiki/Soha_Ali_Khan" title="Soha Ali Khan">Soha Ali Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irrfan_Khan" title="Irrfan Khan">Irrfan Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kay_Kay_Menon" title="Kay Kay Menon">Kay Kay Menon</a> became critically acclaimed with Madhavan's portrayal of a man with a post-traumatic stress disorder being appreciated by reviewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mmjreview2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-mmjreview2-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mmjreview_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-mmjreview-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.932014">2009–2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2009–2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut and R. Madhavan pose for the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="417" data-file-width="355" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg/200px-Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg/300px-Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madhavan with co-star <a href="/wiki/Kangana_Ranaut" title="Kangana Ranaut">Kangana Ranaut</a> at a promotional event for <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i>, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madhavan won positive acclaim for playing the lead role of an engineer experiencing eerie events in Vikram Kumar's bilingual horror film, <i><a href="/wiki/Yavarum_Nalam" title="Yavarum Nalam">Yavarum Nalam</a></i> (2009). The film, which became a commercial and critical success, prompted a reviewer from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Times_of_India" title="Times of India">Times of India</a> to suggest "he carried the film on his shoulders" while he was also nominated in the <a href="/wiki/Vijay_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Vijay Award for Best Actor">Best Actor</a> category at the <a href="/wiki/Vijay_Awards" title="Vijay Awards">Vijay Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ynreviews_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-ynreviews-68">[68]</a></sup> His following two films, the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_En_Aalu" title="Guru En Aalu">Guru En Aalu</a></i> (2009) and the action film <i><a href="/wiki/Sikandar_(2009_film)" title="Sikandar (2009 film)">Sikandar</a></i> (2009) in which he played a supporting role of an army officer, both fetched mixed reviews. Madhavan then portrayed one of three leading roles in <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coming_of_age_film" title="Coming of age film">coming of age</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy_film" title="Comedy film">comedy</a>-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_film" title="Drama film">drama film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> (2009), alongside <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharman_Joshi" title="Sharman Joshi">Sharman Joshi</a>. Upon release, the film received positive reviews and went on to become the highest-grossing Indian film of all time, before being overtaken in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-69">[69]</a></sup> Madhavan's portrayal as a young engineer with a passion for photography earned him nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actor">Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actor</a> and for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IIFA_Best_Supporting_Actor_Award" title="IIFA Best Supporting Actor Award">IIFA Best Supporting Actor Award</a> during 2010. Film critic <a href="/wiki/Taran_Adarsh" title="Taran Adarsh">Taran Adarsh</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a> described the actor's performance as "incredible", while Madhavan claimed that the film changed how he was viewed as an actor in Hindi films for the better.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tireview_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-tireview-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ticahneg_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-ticahneg-71">[71]</a></sup> He later turned down an offer of reprising the same role in the Tamil remake of the film helmed by <a href="/wiki/S._Shankar" title="S. Shankar">Shankar</a>. In 2010, Madhavan appeared alongside actors <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan" title="Amitabh Bachchan">Amitabh Bachchan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Teen_Patti_(film)" title="Teen Patti (film)">Teen Patti</a></i> (2010) as a young professor, with Adarsh again rating his performance as "excellent", but the film failed at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpreview_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-tpreview-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpred_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-tpred-73">[73]</a></sup> His two guest appearances in the year also received mixed feedback with his performance in the Telugu anthology film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Om_Shanti" title="Om Shanti">Om Shanti</a></i> (2010) being praised, whilst a role in the <a href="/wiki/John_Abraham_(actor)" title="John Abraham (actor)">John Abraham</a>-starrer <i><a href="/wiki/Jhootha_Hi_Sahi" title="Jhootha Hi Sahi">Jhootha Hi Sahi</a></i> (2010) drew him criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jhsreview_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-jhsreview-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osid_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-osid-75">[75]</a></sup> Madhavan then collaborated again with <a href="/wiki/Kamal_Haasan" title="Kamal Haasan">Kamal Haasan</a> and <a href="/wiki/K._S._Ravikumar" title="K. S. Ravikumar">K. S. Ravikumar</a> in the romantic comedy, <i><a href="/wiki/Manmadan_Ambu" title="Manmadan Ambu">Manmadan Ambu</a></i> (2010), playing a wealthy businessman who hires a spy to follow his actress girlfriend on a European cruise tour. The film opened to positive reviews with Madhavan's performance being described by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rediff" title="Rediff">Rediff</a>.com as "excellent", while <a href="/wiki/Sify" title="Sify">Sify</a>.com labelled him the "scene stealer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mmareview_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-mmareview-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rediffmmaed_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-rediffmmaed-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>His only release in 2011 was the romantic drama film, <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Kangana_Ranaut" title="Kangana Ranaut">Kangana Ranaut</a>, which saw him play the role of a sensible doctor hoping to get an arranged marriage with a girl, who has a dramatically diverse personality to him. Prior to release, the film's promotional campaign created anticipation and upon release, the film became a large success at the box office. Madhavan's portrayal of Manoj "Manu" Sharma won positive acclaim, with a reviewer citing that his performance was "real, restrained, yet forceful" and another claiming he was "perfectly cast".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twmreview_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-twmreview-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redifftwm_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-redifftwm-79">[79]</a></sup> Madhavan next appeared as a police officer in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N._Linguswamy" title="N. Linguswamy">Linguswamy</a>'s Tamil film <i><a href="/wiki/Vettai" title="Vettai">Vettai</a></i> (2012), an action entertainer featuring an ensemble cast of <a href="/wiki/Arya_(actor)" title="Arya (actor)">Arya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amala_Paul" title="Amala Paul">Amala Paul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sameera_Reddy" title="Sameera Reddy">Sameera Reddy</a>. The film opened to positive reviews in January 2012 and went on to become a commercial success, with critics praising Madhavan's decision to accept the role of a timid cop, while a critic noted that he had "an uncanny talent for comedy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adhir_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-adhir-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vettai_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-vettai-81">[81]</a></sup> He then featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Jodi_Breakers" title="Jodi Breakers">Jodi Breakers</a></i> (2012), a Hindi romantic comedy film shot in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Bipasha_Basu" title="Bipasha Basu">Bipasha Basu</a>, though the film did not perform well commercially.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sff_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-sff-82">[82]</a></sup> In 2012, Madhavan took a sabbatical and was based in Chicago resting his knee, which he injured during the making of <i>Vettai</i>, causing him to suffer from <a href="/wiki/Chondromalacia_patellae" title="Chondromalacia patellae">chondromalacia patellae</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> During the period, he felt he had to "reinvent himself" and had to work on films which would appeal to the "new generation of audiences", so took a decision to work on a single film at a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> During a period of three years without any theatrical releases, his long-delayed Hindi film <i><a href="/wiki/Sunglass_(film)" title="Sunglass (film)">Taak Jhaank</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Rituparno_Ghosh" title="Rituparno Ghosh">Rituparno Ghosh</a> in 2006, premièred at the 19th Kolkata International Film Festival in 2013, while his first Hindi film <i><a href="/wiki/Akeli_(film)" title="Akeli (film)">Akeli</a></i>, shot in 1997, was released online during the following year. During his recovery period and sabbatical in 2013, Madhavan signed on to appear in <a href="/wiki/Simon_West" title="Simon West">Simon West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Night_of_the_Living_Dead:_Darkest_Dawn" title="Night of the Living Dead: Darkest Dawn">Night of the Living Dead: Darkest Dawn</a></i>, in which he appeared as a former marine personnel and shot for the project in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer animated</a> film, where Madhavan provided voice work, premièred in San Diego during July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.93present">2015–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madhavan's first theatrical release after his sabbatical was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anand_L._Rai" title="Anand L. Rai">Anand L. Rai</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu_Returns" title="Tanu Weds Manu Returns">Tanu Weds Manu Returns</a></i>, a sequel to the 2011 film, which released in May 2015. Prior to the film's release, Madhavan stated that the "content of the film was more important than the stars" and acknowledged that the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Kangana_Ranaut" title="Kangana Ranaut">Kangana Ranaut</a> would help the film gain a good opening at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Reprising his role as Manu, Madhavan won acclaim for his restrained performance and the film went on to become a critical and commercial success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The critic from <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a> wrote "Madhavan excels in his role despite it being a restrained one, which was anyways the call of his character" and added "he is very endearing who never tries to overshadow anyone and emerges a winner", while Sify.com stated he gives a "subtle and restrained performance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> <i>Tanu Weds Manu Returns</i> earned <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>243 crore</span> (US$36 million) worldwide at the end of its theatrical run, to become one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Bollywood_films" title="List of highest-grossing Bollywood films">highest-grossing Bollywood films</a> in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240cr_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-240cr-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>During his sabbatical, Madhavan also worked extensively on the pre-production of the bilingual sports film, <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Irudhi Suttru</a></i> (2016) directed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudha_Kongara_Prasad" title="Sudha Kongara Prasad">Sudha Kongara</a>. After being impressed with Sudha's script, he helped find the project producers in Tamil and chose to produce the film in Hindi alongside <a href="/wiki/Y_NOT_Studios" title="Y NOT Studios">Sashikanth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a>. Madhavan also met and convinced <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">mixed martial artist</a> Ritika Singh to act in the film after contacting her through <a href="/wiki/Raj_Kundra" title="Raj Kundra">Raj Kundra</a>, while he was also credited for contributing as an additional screenplay writer. He also went through a body conditioning regime in Los Angeles prior to joining the film's set and learnt boxing to essay the role of a former boxer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> For dubbing purposes, Madhavan wore metal braces inside his teeth, in order to create the effect of having a lisp that most boxers have from sporting injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nie_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-nie-98">[98]</a></sup> Madhavan won praise for his work during the marketing campaign, having travelled throughout <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> to promote the film, with <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a> stating it was "unlike other film promotions in the South".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> For <i>Irudhi Suttru</i>, Madhavan received widespread critical acclaim for his portrayal with Sify.com stating "he is outstanding and carries the proverbial burden of the project on his shoulder".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> A critic from <a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a> stated that he was "quietly effective", while a reviewer from Behindwoods.com wrote that Madhavan gives his "best performance" and is "excellent" at depicting his "characterization from being subtle to being outright effervescent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> His portrayal in the Hindi version, <i>Saala Khadoos</i>, received similar praise with critic <a href="/wiki/Subhash_K._Jha" title="Subhash K. Jha">Subhash K. Jha</a> stating "this is Madhavan’s career-defining performance, he sinks so deep into his role both physically and emotionally, that the actor becomes one with the act".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan has signed on to appear in the Tamil remake of the successful Malayalam film, <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_(2015_Malayalam_film)" title="Charlie (2015 Malayalam film)">Charlie</a></i> (2015), after being impressed by the original. Directed by <a href="/wiki/A._L._Vijay" title="A. L. Vijay">Vijay</a> and produced by Shruti Nallappa, the film will commence production in 2017. Madhavan is also working on <i><a href="/wiki/Vikram_Vedha" title="Vikram Vedha">Vikram Vedha</a></i> directed by duo <a href="/wiki/Pushkar%E2%80%93Gayathri" title="Pushkar–Gayathri">Pushkar–Gayathri</a>, where he portrays an encounter specialist in an ensemble cast also featuring <a href="/wiki/Vijay_Sethupathi" title="Vijay Sethupathi">Vijay Sethupathi</a>. He has confirmed that he would also work on two more bilingual films directed by <a href="/wiki/A._Sarkunam" title="A. Sarkunam">Sarkunam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sangeeth_Sivan" title="Sangeeth Sivan">Sangeeth Sivan</a>, as well as on the Tamil film, <i>Gramophone</i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Karu_Pazhaniappan" title="Karu Pazhaniappan">Karu Pazhaniappan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_projects">Other projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television_work">Film and television work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Film and television work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madhavan was first credited as a part of the technical crew for his work in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramji_Londonwaley" title="Ramji Londonwaley">Ramji Londonwaley</a></i>, an adaptation of his Tamil film <i><a href="/wiki/Nala_Damayanthi" title="Nala Damayanthi">Nala Damayanthi</a></i>. Apart from portraying the lead role, Madhavan worked on the film as a dialogue writer and played an active role in determining the crew of the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rlpick_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-rlpick-107">[107]</a></sup> In October 2007, Madhavan founded the production company, Leukos Films, and consequently bought the rights of his film, <i><a href="/wiki/Evano_Oruvan" title="Evano Oruvan">Evano Oruvan</a></i>, from producers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbas-Mustan" title="Abbas-Mustan">Abbas-Mustan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K._Sera_Sera" title="K. Sera Sera">K. Sera Sera</a>. Securing sponsorship deals with <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> and Santoor, Madhavan premièred the film across North America and the Middle East before its Indian theatrical release, with the promotion method being used for the first time in Tamil cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoprom_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-eoprom-61">[61]</a></sup> However, since the relative box office failure of the project, Madhavan downplayed future involvement in production ventures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noprod_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-noprod-108">[108]</a></sup> The film, which Madhavan referred to as a "part of his life" during 2007, also saw him write the dialogues for the film along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seeman_(director)" title="Seeman (director)">Seeman</a> by translating lines from the project's original version in the <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a> language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eolife_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-eolife-109">[109]</a></sup> Madhavan then chose to become actively involved in the production of his 2016 bilingual films, <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Irudhi Suttru</a></i> in Tamil and <i>Saala Khadoos</i> in Hindi, in order to ensure the film completed filming and had a theatrical release. Impressed by the strength of <a href="/wiki/Sudha_Kongara" title="Sudha Kongara">Sudha Kongara</a>'s script for the Tamil film, Madhavan felt that the story had pan-Indian appeal and took the film's script to <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a>, who agreed to produce and supervise work on the film's Hindi version. Madhavan co-produced the Hindi version of the film through his new production house, Tricolor Films, while leading the film's pan-Indian marketing campaign. The actor also helped finalise the film's lead actress, Ritika Singh, and was also credited as an additional screenplay writer in the films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan has appeared as host for television programmes on <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> channels, while he has also been a host at film award functions. During his television career in the 1990s, Madhavan first worked as a host on <i>Tol Mol Ke Bol</i>. He was announced as the host of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Entertainment" title="Sony Entertainment">Sony Entertainment</a> Television's <i><a href="/wiki/Deal_Ya_No_Deal" title="Deal Ya No Deal">Deal Ya No Deal</a></i>, the Indian version of the American game show <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deal_Or_No_Deal" title="Deal Or No Deal">Deal Or No Deal</a></i>, in October 2005. However, Madhavan quit as the lead anchor of the show in January 2006 claiming he was unhappy with the way the shoot schedules were handled by the production house. According to the actor, when he took on the show, he had made it clear that he would continue with his South Indian film assignments, and as the show was being filmed in Mumbai, he had found it hard to keep travelling throughout India from Chennai to film the ten days a month he had signed up for. Madhavan added that he was restricted by the producers to spend one day rehearsing technically, which left him with fatigue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thambi_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-thambi-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mandira_Bedi" title="Mandira Bedi">Mandira Bedi</a> subsequently replaced Madhavan as the anchor in February for Series 2 of the game show. In June 2010, Madhavan made a comeback to the game show format by accepting a contract with Imagine TV's Big Money show, signing on to host a single season, and then hosted an episode of the crime show <a href="/wiki/Savdhaan_India" title="Savdhaan India">Savdhaan India</a> in January 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-left_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-left-112">[112]</a></sup> Furthermore, he has been a guest judge in the Indian television show, <a href="/wiki/Fame_Gurukul" title="Fame Gurukul">Fame Gurukul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gurukul_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-gurukul-113">[113]</a></sup> In 2016, Madhavan stated that he would only take part in television commitments for money, while he does not consider his payment when signing on to appear in films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Madhavan has also hosted live events, notably the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Awards</a> in 2013 with <a href="/wiki/Huma_Qureshi_(actress)" title="Huma Qureshi (actress)">Huma Qureshi</a>. He was also the host of the 55th <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards_South" title="Filmfare Awards South">Filmfare Awards South</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> in 2008 and then also the Vijay Awards in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ffhosr_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-ffhosr-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_ambassador">Brand ambassador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Brand ambassador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madhavan is amongst the leading brand ambassadors for products in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> His early work involved advertisements for brands including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bajaj_group" title="Bajaj group">Bajaj</a>, Ponds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_and_Lovely" title="Fair and Lovely">Fair and Lovely</a> and <a href="/wiki/TVS_Group" title="TVS Group">TVS</a>, before signing a major endorsing deal with <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> and marketing company, IMG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-img_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-img-118">[118]</a></sup> In 2007, Madhavan endorsed UniverCell, a multi-brand mobile phone retail chain owned by UniverCell Telecommunications India Pvt Ltd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Madhavan signed a contract with the mobile phone network, <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Airtel</a> for promotions in South India before being promoted as the pan-Indian ambassador for the brand a year later. His advertisements with <a href="/wiki/Vidya_Balan" title="Vidya Balan">Vidya Balan</a> for Airtel won critical acclaim, and brought in film offers for the pair to feature together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airtel_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-airtel-120">[120]</a></sup> In June 2010, marketers from Arun Excello promoted a housing project in Oragadam, Chennai in a similar fashion to the release of a new film featuring Madhavan. With film-inspired posters and billboards put up around Chennai, the advertisement campaign attracted huge curiosity and the project became a success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orohiy_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-orohiy-121">[121]</a></sup> His long-term work with jewellery brand, <a href="/wiki/Joyalukkas" title="Joyalukkas">Joy Alukkas</a>, led to the company creating life size wax models of him to place in their showrooms from January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wax_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-wax-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maruti_Suzuki" title="Maruti Suzuki">Maruti Suzuki</a>, for whom Madhavan is the brand ambassador, launched a special edition of the <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Wagon_R" title="Suzuki Wagon R">Suzuki Wagon R</a> car calling it the Madhavan Signature Edition in September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maruti_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-maruti-123">[123]</a></sup> In 2015, online market place Snapdeal signed on <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a> and Madhavan to be the company's ambassadors, with Snapdeal attempting to use Madhavan's popularity in South India to marker their services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_causes">Humanitarian causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Humanitarian causes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madhavan, who is a vegetarian, endorses the brand, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA">PETA</a>. Since joining them after starring in his first film, he has appeared voluntarily in several advertisements and released an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interactive" title="Interactive">E-Card</a> for the brand. In July 2006, Madhavan was voted the "cutest male vegetarian" by an online poll conducted by the NGO, People for Ethical Treatment of Animals (PETA), while <a href="/wiki/Kareena_Kapoor" title="Kareena Kapoor">Kareena Kapoor</a> won the female award respectively. In turn he cited that his success in the competition was due to his "healthy vegetarian diet".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vege_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-vege-125">[125]</a></sup> In October 2010, he wrote a letter to the CEO of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kentucky_Fried_Chicken" title="Kentucky Fried Chicken">Kentucky Fried Chicken</a>, on behalf of PETA, urging them to stop mistreatment of birds by the fast-food industry outlets and the killing of animals. He requested the boycott of KFC in India over animal welfare and conditions and was joined by <a href="/wiki/Raveena_Tandon" title="Raveena Tandon">Raveena Tandon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rakhi_Sawant" title="Rakhi Sawant">Rakhi Sawant</a> in supporting the work of PETA in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kfc_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-kfc-126">[126]</a></sup> In addition, Madhavan was named PETA India’s 2012 "Person Of The Year", while his son won PETA India's "Compassionate Kid award" in December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan has lent his support for the Chennai-based charity, The Banyan, and appeared in the charity musical <a href="/wiki/Netru,_Indru,_Naalai" title="Netru, Indru, Naalai">Netru, Indru, Naalai</a> directed by Mani Ratnam for the cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ninbanyan_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-ninbanyan-128">[128]</a></sup> He appeared as a guest cook and newly launched restaurant in Chennai and cooked <a href="/wiki/Dosa" title="Dosa">dosas</a> for auction for the charity, helping raise forty five thousand rupees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cookhelp_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-cookhelp-129">[129]</a></sup> He has been a part of an AIDS awareness programme initiated by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gere" title="Richard Gere">Richard Gere</a> in India and helped advertise the <i>A Time for Heroes</i> campaign appearing in a short film. Similarly Madhavan featured in a four-minute film produced by Agaram Foundation, <i><a href="/wiki/Herova%3F_Zerova%3F" title="Herova? Zerova?">Herova? Zerova?</a></i>, campaigning for educational awareness alongside <a href="/wiki/Suriya" title="Suriya">Suriya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vijay_(actor)" title="Vijay (actor)">Vijay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jyothika" title="Jyothika">Jyothika</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In 2010, along with his cast and crew from <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i>, he helped raise Rs. 2.5 million for the renovation of the school in <a href="/wiki/Leh" title="Leh">Leh</a>, which was damaged by flash floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Madhavan laid bricks and tiles at the <a href="/wiki/London_Business_School" title="London Business School">London Business School</a> in July 2011, building a symbolic house to represent the 100,000 houses that will be built in India by 2015 as a part of Habitat for Humanity's campaign to improve substandard houses in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2015_South_Indian_floods" title="2015 South Indian floods">2015 South Indian floods</a>, Madhavan worked alongside other Indian actors in coordinating the relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Lepra" title="Lepra">Lepra India</a> signed him to work as a goodwill ambassador in helping promote action against leprosy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: In the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madhavanff.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="464" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Madhavanff.JPG/220px-Madhavanff.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Madhavanff.JPG/330px-Madhavanff.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Madhavanff.JPG/440px-Madhavanff.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madhavanff.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madhavan seen with his wife, Sarita, at the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> ceremony in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madhavan is one of the few actors in India who garners pan-Indian appeal, with his success in establishing himself in the North and the South Indian film industries, seeing him receive multiple offers as a brand ambassador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-img_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-img-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Furthermore, it has led to producers offering him lead roles in bilingual films such as the English-Malayalam crossover film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nothing_But_Life" title="Nothing But Life">Nothing But Life</a></i> and the Hindi-Tamil projects, <i><a href="/wiki/Yavarum_Nalam" title="Yavarum Nalam">Yavarum Nalam</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Irudhi Suttru</a></i>. Moreover, most of his Tamil films are dubbed into Telugu, where he has created a box office market without appearing in a single straight Telugu film as a lead actor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telugusuc_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-telugusuc-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teluglang_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-teluglang-140">[140]</a></sup> Madhavan holds a significant female fan following, which developed after his romantic roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Alaipayuthey" title="Alaipayuthey">Alaipayuthey</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Minnale" title="Minnale">Minnale</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Madhavan has also been active in keeping in contact with fans, maintaining a fan email account, a Facebook fan page and a Twitter account as well as being one of the first actors of Tamil films to turn blogger with entries in the year 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blog_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-blog-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>He has appeared at functions as a special guest, and has enjoyed particularly close links with technology company, <a href="/wiki/Sify" title="Sify">Sify</a>, whom he signed on as his media partner for all his future releases after expressing satisfaction at the website they created for <i><a href="/wiki/Rendu" title="Rendu">Rendu</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sifmax_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-sifmax-144">[144]</a></sup> Madhavan sat amongst a six-man jury for the selection of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN-IBN" title="CNN-IBN">IBN</a> Indian of the Year 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibn_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-gibn-145">[145]</a></sup> He inaugurated the Chennai International Film Festival in 2007, taking the opportunity to deliver a message on preserving the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciff_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-ciff-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>A gaming company, Paradox Studios Limited, launched a new game compatible with mobile phones in July 2006, with Madhavan as the lead character. The company released two mobile game titles featuring Madhavan as their lead character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-game_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-game-147">[147]</a></sup> The first of the two games, <i>Madhavan's MIG</i>, featured the actor making a reprise of his <a href="/wiki/Rang_De_Basanti" title="Rang De Basanti">Rang De Basanti</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aviator" title="Aviator">pilot</a>'s role. In the other game titled <i>Madhavan</i>, the player had to help the actor get to the première of his latest movie evading the paparazzi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gametwo_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-gametwo-148">[148]</a></sup> In 2007, prominent entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/N._R._Narayana_Murthy" title="N. R. Narayana Murthy">N. R. Narayana Murthy</a> requested Madhavan to be his interviewer at the India-Singapore Exposition and Madhavan went on to claim that the experience was "unforgettable" as Murthy was an idol to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murthy_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-murthy-149">[149]</a></sup> Madhavan has also attended conferences as a motivational speaker, talking about issues including situational awareness and confidence, with a speech delivered at <a href="/wiki/Dr_G_R_Damodaran_College_of_Science" title="Dr G R Damodaran College of Science">Damodaran Academy of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore" title="Coimbatore">Coimbatore</a> going viral online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=R._Madhavan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Madhavan's parents are Ranganathan Seshadri and Saroja. Despite Madhavan's ambition of wanting to join the army, his parents insisted he go to management school and pursue a degree in <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-family_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-family-6">[6]</a></sup> After completing the degree, he went on to teach communication and public speaking at workshops around India. At the <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> workshop, he encountered his wife Sarita Birje for the first time during 1991, when she attended his class on the recommendation of her cousins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ens_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-ens-151">[151]</a></sup> Sarita was able to use the skills she had learned from Madhavan's classes to pass an interview to become an air hostess and after completing the course, the pair began dating. They later married in 1999, before Madhavan entered mainstream films. The pair's successful marriage has been covered by the media, with Madhavan citing that advise from his mentor <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a> was useful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twm2015_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-twm2015-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marriage_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-marriage-152">[152]</a></sup> Sarita has worked as a costume designer in a few of Madhavan's films, most notably for <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_En_Aalu" title="Guru En Aalu">Guru En Aalu</a></i> (2009) when she worked along with <a href="/wiki/Erum_Ali" title="Erum Ali">Erum Ali</a>, the wife of Madhavan's co-star, <a href="/wiki/Abbas_(actor)" title="Abbas (actor)">Abbas</a>, for their respective husbands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-designe_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-designe-153">[153]</a></sup> Their son, Vedant was born in August 2005, which eventually led to relocating to the boat-club area in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kilpauk" title="Kilpauk">Kilpauk</a>, where Madhavan's parents lived with him as well as his parents-in-law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vedant_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-vedant-154">[154]</a></sup> In 2009, he relocated to <a href="/wiki/Kandivali" title="Kandivali">Kandivali</a>, Mumbai with his wife and son, as he pursued a career in <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> films ahead of films in the South Indian industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan has maintained close links with fellow actors and has described actor <a href="/wiki/Suriya" title="Suriya">Suriya</a> as his best friend in the film industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The actor also is close friends with actresses <a href="/wiki/Shilpa_Shetty" title="Shilpa Shetty">Shilpa Shetty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bipasha_Basu" title="Bipasha Basu">Bipasha Basu</a>, as well as actors <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Bachchan" title="Abhishek Bachchan">Abhishek Bachchan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> He is closely associated with actor <a href="/wiki/Kamal_Haasan" title="Kamal Haasan">Kamal Haasan</a>, after their appearance together in <i><a href="/wiki/Anbe_Sivam" title="Anbe Sivam">Anbe Sivam</a></i>, and has revealed that he considers the actor as his inspiration. He has also collaborated multiple times with directors Mani Ratnam, <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aanand_Rai" title="Aanand Rai">Aanand Rai</a>, citing that the film makers "understand him well" and share a good "comfort level". He has also helped out actresses <a href="/wiki/Reemma_Sen" title="Reemma Sen">Reemma Sen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sadha" title="Sadha">Sadha</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nisha_Kothari" title="Nisha Kothari">Nisha Kothari</a> by signing them on for roles in his films, when they were going through a barren spell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nishak_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-nishak-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reema_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-reema-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadha_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadha-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Madhavan announced a sabbatical from films in late 2010 citing he would take the time off to visit London, lose weight, play golf, take treatment for his knee injury and spend time with family. Though he kept away from starting new projects, during the period he was involved in the promotional activity of two of his releases, <i><a href="/wiki/Manmadan_Ambu" title="Manmadan Ambu">Manmadan Ambu</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sabbatical_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-sabbatical-162">[162]</a></sup> He later made a comeback, earlier than anticipated, after director <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N._Linguswamy" title="N. Linguswamy">Linguswamy</a> convinced him to work on <i><a href="/wiki/Vettai" title="Vettai">Vettai</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> The actor later took an extended sabbatical from 2012 onwards to work on his fitness and get into shape for his role as a retired boxer in <i><a href="/wiki/Irudhi_Suttru" title="Irudhi Suttru">Irudhi Suttru</a></i>. Madhavan is a keen golf player, having played for pleasure alongside actor <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan" title="Amitabh Bachchan">Amitabh Bachchan</a> and director <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a>, while also appearing in a celebrity charity event in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-golf_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-golf-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> He also made an appearance for Chennai Rhinos in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Celebrity_Cricket_League" title="2011 Celebrity Cricket League">2011 Celebrity Cricket League</a>, playing against Karnataka Bulldozers. His experiences flying Cessna planes when he was with National Cadet Corps, also led to a passion for aero-modelling, with the actor stating it "justified his decision" to pursue a degree in electronics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aeromodel_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-aeromodel-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
